<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Michael Jordan</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<div id="contentSub2"></div>

<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">American basketball player and businessman</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the American basketball player. For other people with the same name, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Michael_Jordan_(disambiguation)" title="Michael Jordan (disambiguation)">Michael Jordan (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<li><a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s_All-American_Game" title="McDonald's All-American Game">McDonald's All-American</a> (<a href="/wiki/1981_McDonald%27s_All-American_Boys_Game" title="1981 McDonald's All-American Boys Game">1981</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a> (2016)</li></ul>
</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><th colspan="2">
</th></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#00788C;color:#FFFFFF;border:2.5px solid #1D1160;">Career NBA  statistics</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="text-align: right; line-height: 1.2em"><a href="/wiki/Point_(basketball)" title="Point (basketball)">Points</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.2em">32,292 (30.1 ppg)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="text-align: right; line-height: 1.2em"><a href="/wiki/Rebound_(basketball)" title="Rebound (basketball)">Rebounds</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.2em">6,672 (6.2 rpg)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="text-align: right; line-height: 1.2em"><a href="/wiki/Assist_(basketball)" title="Assist (basketball)">Assists</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.2em">5,633 (5.3 apg)</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><th colspan="2">

<p><b>Michael Jeffrey Jordan</b> (born February 17, 1963), also known by his initials <b>MJ</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup> is a businessman and retired American former professional <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> player. He is the principal owner and chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Hornets" title="Charlotte Hornets">Charlotte Hornets</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a> (NBA) and of <a href="/wiki/23XI_Racing" title="23XI Racing">23XI Racing</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nascar_Cup_Series" title="Nascar Cup Series">Nascar Cup Series</a>. He played 15 seasons in the NBA, winning six championships with the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bulls" title="Chicago Bulls">Chicago Bulls</a>. His biography on the official <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA" title="NBA">NBA</a> website states: "By acclamation, Michael Jordan is the greatest basketball player of all time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup> He was integral in helping to popularize the NBA around the world in the 1980s and 1990s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Markovits_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Markovits-11">[9]</a></sup> becoming a global <a href="/wiki/Cultural_icon" title="Cultural icon">cultural icon</a> in the process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faze.ca_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-faze.ca-12">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jordan played <a href="/wiki/College_basketball" title="College basketball">college basketball</a> for three seasons under coach <a href="/wiki/Dean_Smith" title="Dean Smith">Dean Smith</a> with the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_men%27s_basketball" title="North Carolina Tar Heels men's basketball">North Carolina Tar Heels</a>. As a freshman, he was a member of the Tar Heels' national championship team in <a href="/wiki/1982_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="1982 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament">1982</a>. Jordan joined the Bulls in <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_NBA_season" title="1984–85 NBA season">1984</a> as the third overall draft pick, and quickly emerged as a league star, entertaining crowds with his prolific scoring while gaining a reputation as one of the game's best defensive players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-defensive_players_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-defensive_players-13">[11]</a></sup> His leaping ability, demonstrated by performing <a href="/wiki/Slam_dunk" title="Slam dunk">slam dunks</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_throw_line" title="Free throw line">free throw line</a> in <a href="/wiki/Slam_Dunk_Contest" title="Slam Dunk Contest">Slam Dunk Contests</a>, earned him the nicknames "<b>Air Jordan</b>" and "<b>His Airness</b>". Jordan won his first NBA championship with the Bulls in 1991, and followed that achievement with titles in 1992 and 1993, securing a "<a href="/wiki/Three-peat" title="Three-peat">three-peat</a>". Jordan abruptly retired from basketball before the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_NBA_season" title="1993–94 NBA season">1993–94 NBA season</a> to play <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">Minor League Baseball</a>, but returned to the Bulls in March 1995 and led them to three more championships in 1996, 1997, and 1998, as well as a then-record 72 regular-season wins in the 1995–96 NBA season. He retired for a second time in January 1999 but returned for two more NBA seasons from 2001 to 2003 as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Wizards" title="Washington Wizards">Washington Wizards</a>.
</p><p>Jordan's individual accolades and accomplishments include six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bill_Russell_NBA_Finals_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Bill Russell NBA Finals Most Valuable Player Award">NBA Finals Most Valuable Player (MVP) Awards</a>, ten <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Basketball_Association_annual_scoring_leaders" title="List of National Basketball Association annual scoring leaders">scoring titles</a> (both all-time records), five <a href="/wiki/NBA_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="NBA Most Valuable Player Award">MVP Awards</a>, ten <a href="/wiki/All-NBA_Team" title="All-NBA Team">All-NBA</a> First Team designations, nine <a href="/wiki/NBA_All-Defensive_Team" title="NBA All-Defensive Team">All-Defensive</a> First Team honors, fourteen <a href="/wiki/NBA_All-Star_Game" title="NBA All-Star Game">NBA All-Star Game</a> selections, three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA_All-Star_Game_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="NBA All-Star Game Most Valuable Player Award">All-Star Game MVP Awards</a>, three <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Basketball_Association_annual_steals_leaders" title="List of National Basketball Association annual steals leaders">steals titles</a>, and the 1988 <a href="/wiki/NBA_Defensive_Player_of_the_Year_Award" title="NBA Defensive Player of the Year Award">NBA Defensive Player of the Year Award</a>. He holds the NBA records for career regular season scoring average (30.12 points per game) and  career playoff scoring average (33.45 points per game). In 1999, he was named the 20th century's greatest North American athlete by <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>, and was second to <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a>' list of athletes of the century. Jordan was twice inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Naismith_Memorial_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame">Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame</a>, once in 2009 for his individual career and again in 2010 as part of the <a href="/wiki/1992_United_States_men%27s_Olympic_basketball_team" title="1992 United States men's Olympic basketball team">1992 United States men's Olympic basketball team</a> ("The Dream Team"). He became a member of the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Hall_of_Fame" title="FIBA Hall of Fame">FIBA Hall of Fame</a> in 2015.
</p><p>One of the most effectively marketed athletes of his generation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Markovits_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Markovits-11">[9]</a></sup> Jordan is also known for his product endorsements. He fueled the success of <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Air_Jordan" title="Air Jordan">Air Jordan</a> sneakers, which were introduced in 1984 and remain popular today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-remain_popular_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-remain_popular-14">[12]</a></sup> Jordan also starred as himself in the 1996 film <i><a href="/wiki/Space_Jam" title="Space Jam">Space Jam</a></i>. He became part-owner and head of basketball operations for the Charlotte Bobcats (now named the Hornets) in 2006, and bought a controlling interest in 2010. In 2014, Jordan became the first billionaire player in NBA history. With a net worth of $2.1 billion, he is the fourth-richest African American, behind <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Smith_(investor)" title="Robert F. Smith (investor)">Robert F. Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Steward" title="David Steward">David Steward</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oprah_Winfrey" title="Oprah Winfrey">Oprah Winfrey</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Michael Jeffrey Jordan was born at Cumberland Hospital in the <a href="/wiki/Fort_Greene,_Brooklyn" title="Fort Greene, Brooklyn">Fort Greene</a> neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a> borough on February 17, 1963,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brooklyn_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brooklyn-15">[13]</a></sup> the son of bank employee Deloris (née Peoples) and equipment supervisor <a href="/wiki/James_R._Jordan_Sr." title="James R. Jordan Sr.">James R. Jordan Sr.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brooklyn_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Brooklyn-15">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup> In 1968, he moved with his family to <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_North_Carolina" title="Wilmington, North Carolina">Wilmington, North Carolina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup> Jordan attended <a href="/wiki/Emsley_A._Laney_High_School" title="Emsley A. Laney High School">Emsley A. Laney High School</a> in Wilmington, where he highlighted his athletic career by playing basketball, baseball, and football. He tried out for the <a href="/wiki/Varsity_team" title="Varsity team">varsity</a> basketball team during his sophomore year but, at 5'11" (1.80 m), he was deemed too short to play at that level. His taller friend, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harvest_Smith" title="Harvest Smith">Harvest Leroy Smith</a>, was the only sophomore to make the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-halb_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-halb-18">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-varsity_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-varsity-19">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>Motivated to prove his worth, Jordan became the star of Laney's <a href="/wiki/Junior_varsity_team" title="Junior varsity team">junior varsity team</a>, and tallied several 40-point games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-halb_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-halb-18">[16]</a></sup> The following summer, he grew four inches (10 cm) and trained rigorously.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-varsity_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-varsity-19">[17]</a></sup> Upon earning a spot on the varsity roster, Jordan averaged more than 25 <a href="/wiki/Points_per_game" title="Points per game">points per game</a> (ppg) over his final two seasons of high school play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-school_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-school-20">[18]</a></sup> As a senior, he was selected to play in the <a href="/wiki/1981_McDonald%27s_All-American_Boys_Game" title="1981 McDonald's All-American Boys Game">1981 McDonald's All-American Game</a> and scored 30 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McDonald's_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-McDonald's-21">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup> after averaging 27 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-school_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-school-20">[18]</a></sup> 12 <a href="/wiki/Rebound_(basketball)" title="Rebound (basketball)">rebounds</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lazenby_p141_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-lazenby_p141-24">[22]</a></sup> and 6 <a href="/wiki/Assist_(basketball)" title="Assist (basketball)">assists</a> per game for the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lazenby_p141_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-lazenby_p141-24">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> Jordan was recruited by numerous college basketball programs, including <a href="/wiki/Duke_Blue_Devils_men%27s_basketball" title="Duke Blue Devils men's basketball">Duke</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_men%27s_basketball" title="North Carolina Tar Heels men's basketball">North Carolina</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Gamecocks_men%27s_basketball" title="South Carolina Gamecocks men's basketball">South Carolina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_Orange_men%27s_basketball" title="Syracuse Orange men's basketball">Syracuse</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Cavaliers_men%27s_basketball" title="Virginia Cavaliers men's basketball">Virginia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> In 1981, he accepted a basketball scholarship to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill" title="University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill">University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill</a>, where he majored in <a href="/wiki/Cultural_geography" title="Cultural geography">cultural geography</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="College_career">College career</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;max-width:312px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:120px;max-width:120px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:169px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michael_Jordan_-_Laney_High_School_1980_-_02.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="301" data-file-width="209" decoding="async" height="170" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4a/Michael_Jordan_-_Laney_High_School_1980_-_02.jpg 2x" width="118"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Jordan going in for a slam dunk for the Laney High School varsity basketball team, 1979–80</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:188px;max-width:188px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:169px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michael_Jordan_UNC_Jersey_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="728" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Michael_Jordan_UNC_Jersey_cropped.jpg/186px-Michael_Jordan_UNC_Jersey_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Michael_Jordan_UNC_Jersey_cropped.jpg/279px-Michael_Jordan_UNC_Jersey_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Michael_Jordan_UNC_Jersey_cropped.jpg/372px-Michael_Jordan_UNC_Jersey_cropped.jpg 2x" width="186"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Jordan's number 23 jersey among others in the rafters of the <a href="/wiki/Dean_Smith_Center" title="Dean Smith Center">Dean Smith Center</a>, pictured in May 2005</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>As a freshman in coach <a href="/wiki/Dean_Smith" title="Dean Smith">Dean Smith</a>'s team-oriented system, he was named <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">ACC</a> Freshman of the Year after he averaged 13.4 ppg on 53.4% shooting (<a href="/wiki/Field_goal_percentage" title="Field goal percentage">field goal percentage</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbb_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-dbb-29">[27]</a></sup> He made the game-winning jump shot in the <a href="/wiki/1982_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Championship_Game" title="1982 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Championship Game">1982 NCAA Championship game</a> against <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball" title="Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball">Georgetown</a>, which was led by future NBA rival <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Ewing" title="Patrick Ewing">Patrick Ewing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup> Jordan later described this shot as the major turning point in his basketball career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> During his three seasons with the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_men%27s_basketball" title="North Carolina Tar Heels men's basketball">Tar Heels</a>, he averaged 17.7 ppg on 54.0% shooting, and added 5.0 rpg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-br_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-br-31">[29]</a></sup> He was selected by consensus to the <a href="/wiki/1983_NCAA_Men%27s_Basketball_All-Americans" title="1983 NCAA Men's Basketball All-Americans">NCAA All-American First Team</a> in both his sophomore (1983) and junior (1984) seasons. After winning the <a href="/wiki/Naismith_College_Player_of_the_Year" title="Naismith College Player of the Year">Naismith</a> and the <a href="/wiki/John_R._Wooden_Award" title="John R. Wooden Award">Wooden</a> College Player of the Year awards in 1984, Jordan left North Carolina one year before his scheduled graduation to enter the <a href="/wiki/1984_NBA_draft" title="1984 NBA draft">1984 NBA draft</a>. Jordan returned to North Carolina to complete his degree in 1986,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup> when he graduated with a Bachelor of Arts degree in geography.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_career">Professional career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="Early_NBA_years_.281984.E2.80.931987.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_NBA_years_(1984–1987)">Early NBA years (1984–1987)</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_Chicago_Bulls_season" title="1984–85 Chicago Bulls season">Chicago Bulls</a> selected Jordan with the third overall pick of the <a href="/wiki/1984_NBA_draft" title="1984 NBA draft">1984 NBA draft</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Hakeem_Olajuwon" title="Hakeem Olajuwon">Hakeem Olajuwon</a> (<a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_Houston_Rockets_season" title="1984–85 Houston Rockets season">Houston Rockets</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Sam_Bowie" title="Sam Bowie">Sam Bowie</a> (<a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_Portland_Trail_Blazers_season" title="1984–85 Portland Trail Blazers season">Portland Trail Blazers</a>). One of the primary reasons why Jordan was not drafted sooner was because the first two teams were in need of a <a href="/wiki/Center_(basketball)" title="Center (basketball)">center</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> However, Trail Blazers general manager <a href="/wiki/Stu_Inman" title="Stu Inman">Stu Inman</a> contended that it was not a matter of drafting a center, but more a matter of taking Sam Bowie over Jordan, in part because Portland already had <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Drexler" title="Clyde Drexler">Clyde Drexler</a>, who was a guard with similar skills to Jordan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>, citing Bowie's injury-laden college career, named the Blazers' choice of Bowie as the worst draft pick in North American professional sports history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup>
</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_NBA_season" title="1984–85 NBA season">his rookie season</a> with the Bulls, Jordan averaged 28.2 ppg on 51.5% shooting,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbb_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-dbb-29">[27]</a></sup> and helped make a team that had won 35% of games in the previous three seasons playoff contenders. He quickly became a fan favorite even in opposing arenas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gross_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gross-37">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garden_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Garden-39">[37]</a></sup> Roy S. Johnson of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> described him as "the phenomenal rookie of the Bulls" in November,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garden_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Garden-39">[37]</a></sup> and Jordan appeared on the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> with the heading "A Star Is Born" in December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup> The fans also voted in Jordan as an <a href="/wiki/NBA_All-Star_Game" title="NBA All-Star Game">All-Star</a> starter during his rookie season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup> Controversy arose before the All-Star game when word surfaced that several veteran players—led by <a href="/wiki/Isiah_Thomas" title="Isiah Thomas">Isiah Thomas</a>—were upset by the amount of attention Jordan was receiving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup> This led to a so-called "freeze-out" on Jordan, where players refused to pass the ball to him throughout the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-6"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup> The controversy left Jordan relatively unaffected when he returned to regular season play, and he would go on to be voted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA_Rookie_of_the_Year" title="NBA Rookie of the Year">Rookie of the Year</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nba.combio_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-nba.combio-42">[40]</a></sup> The Bulls finished the season 38–44<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbbulls_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-dbbulls-43">[41]</a></sup> and lost to the <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_Milwaukee_Bucks_season" title="1984–85 Milwaukee Bucks season">Milwaukee Bucks</a> in four games in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1985_NBA_Playoffs" title="1985 NBA Playoffs">first round of the playoffs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nba.combio_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-nba.combio-42">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jordan's <a href="/wiki/1985%E2%80%9386_NBA_season" title="1985–86 NBA season">second season</a> was cut short when he broke his foot in the third game of the year, causing him to miss 64 games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-7"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup> The Bulls made the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1986_NBA_Playoffs" title="1986 NBA Playoffs">playoffs</a> despite Jordan's injury and a 30–52 record, at the time the fifth worst record of any team to qualify for the playoffs in NBA history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbbulls_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-dbbulls-43">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup> Jordan recovered in time to participate in the postseason and performed well upon his return. Against a <a href="/wiki/1985%E2%80%9386_Boston_Celtics_season" title="1985–86 Boston Celtics season">1985–86 Boston Celtics team</a> that is often considered one of the greatest in NBA history,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-topteams_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-topteams-45">[43]</a></sup> Jordan set the still-unbroken record for points in a playoff game with 63 in Game 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbadisguised_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-nbadisguised-46">[44]</a></sup> The Celtics, however, managed to sweep the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nba.combio_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-nba.combio-42">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jordan had completely recovered in time for the <a href="/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_NBA_season" title="1986–87 NBA season">1986–87 season</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> and he had one of the most prolific scoring seasons in NBA history. He became the only player other than <a href="/wiki/Wilt_Chamberlain" title="Wilt Chamberlain">Wilt Chamberlain</a> to score 3,000 points in a season, averaging a league high 37.1 points on 48.2% shooting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbb_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-dbb-29">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> In addition, Jordan demonstrated his defensive prowess, as he became the first player in NBA history to record 200 steals and 100 <a href="/wiki/Block_(basketball)" title="Block (basketball)">blocked shots</a> in a season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WashingtonPost05-26-1988_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-WashingtonPost05-26-1988-49">[47]</a></sup> Despite Jordan's success, <a href="/wiki/Magic_Johnson" title="Magic Johnson">Magic Johnson</a> won the league's <a href="/wiki/NBA_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="NBA Most Valuable Player Award">Most Valuable Player Award</a>. The Bulls reached 40 wins,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbbulls_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-dbbulls-43">[41]</a></sup> and advanced to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1987_NBA_Playoffs" title="1987 NBA Playoffs">the playoffs</a> for the third consecutive year. However, they were again swept by the <a href="/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_Boston_Celtics_season" title="1986–87 Boston Celtics season">Celtics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nba.combio_42-3"><a href="#cite_note-nba.combio-42">[40]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Pistons_roadblock_.281987.E2.80.931990.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Pistons_roadblock_(1987–1990)">Pistons roadblock (1987–1990)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BudLightDaredevils_and_Michael_Jordan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="572" data-file-width="720" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/BudLightDaredevils_and_Michael_Jordan.jpg/220px-BudLightDaredevils_and_Michael_Jordan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/BudLightDaredevils_and_Michael_Jordan.jpg/330px-BudLightDaredevils_and_Michael_Jordan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/BudLightDaredevils_and_Michael_Jordan.jpg/440px-BudLightDaredevils_and_Michael_Jordan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BudLightDaredevils_and_Michael_Jordan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jordan (center) in 1987</div></div></div>
<p>Jordan again led the league in scoring during the <a href="/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_NBA_season" title="1987–88 NBA season">1987–88 season</a>, averaging 35.0 ppg on 53.5% shooting<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbb_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-dbb-29">[27]</a></sup> and won his first league MVP Award. He was also named the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA_Defensive_Player_of_the_Year" title="NBA Defensive Player of the Year">Defensive Player of the Year</a>, as he had averaged 1.6 blocks and a league high 3.16 steals per game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MJ_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-MJ-50">[48]</a></sup> The Bulls finished 50–32,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbbulls_43-3"><a href="#cite_note-dbbulls-43">[41]</a></sup> and made it out of the first round of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1988_NBA_Playoffs" title="1988 NBA Playoffs">the playoffs</a> for the first time in Jordan's career, as they defeated the <a href="/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_Cleveland_Cavaliers_season" title="1987–88 Cleveland Cavaliers season">Cleveland Cavaliers</a> in five games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup> However, the Bulls then lost in five games to the more experienced <a href="/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_Detroit_Pistons_season" title="1987–88 Detroit Pistons season">Detroit Pistons</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nba.combio_42-4"><a href="#cite_note-nba.combio-42">[40]</a></sup> who were led by <a href="/wiki/Isiah_Thomas" title="Isiah Thomas">Isiah Thomas</a> and a group of physical players known as the "<a href='/wiki/Detroit_Pistons#1980–1991:_The_"Bad_Boys"_era' title="Detroit Pistons">Bad Boys</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_NBA_season" title="1988–89 NBA season">1988–89 season</a>, Jordan again led the league in scoring, averaging 32.5 ppg on 53.8% shooting from the field, along with 8 rpg and 8 apg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbb_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-dbb-29">[27]</a></sup> The Bulls finished with a 47–35 record,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbbulls_43-4"><a href="#cite_note-dbbulls-43">[41]</a></sup> and advanced to the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Conference_(NBA)" title="Eastern Conference (NBA)">Eastern Conference</a> Finals, defeating the <a href="/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_Cleveland_Cavaliers_season" title="1988–89 Cleveland Cavaliers season">Cavaliers</a> and <a href="/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_New_York_Knicks_season" title="1988–89 New York Knicks season">New York Knicks</a> along the way. The Cavaliers series included a career highlight for Jordan when he hit <i><a href="/wiki/The_Shot" title="The Shot">The Shot</a></i> over <a href="/wiki/Craig_Ehlo" title="Craig Ehlo">Craig Ehlo</a> at the buzzer in the fifth and final game of the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_Detroit_Pistons_season" title="1988–89 Detroit Pistons season">Pistons</a> again defeated the Bulls, this time in six games,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nba.combio_42-5"><a href="#cite_note-nba.combio-42">[40]</a></sup> by utilizing their "<a href="/wiki/Jordan_Rules" title="Jordan Rules">Jordan Rules</a>" method of guarding Jordan, which consisted of <a href="/wiki/Double_team" title="Double team">double and triple teaming</a> him every time he touched the ball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-8"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Bulls entered the <a href="/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_NBA_season" title="1989–90 NBA season">1989–90 season</a> as a team on the rise, with their core group of Jordan and young improving players like <a href="/wiki/Scottie_Pippen" title="Scottie Pippen">Scottie Pippen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Horace_Grant" title="Horace Grant">Horace Grant</a>, and under the guidance of new coach <a href="/wiki/Phil_Jackson" title="Phil Jackson">Phil Jackson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> On March 28, 1990, Jordan scored a career-high 69 points in a 117–113 road win over the Cavaliers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> He averaged a league leading 33.6 ppg on 52.6% shooting, to go with 6.9 rpg and 6.3 apg<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbb_29-5"><a href="#cite_note-dbb-29">[27]</a></sup> in leading the Bulls to a 55–27 record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbbulls_43-5"><a href="#cite_note-dbbulls-43">[41]</a></sup> They again advanced to the Eastern Conference Finals after beating the <a href="/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_Milwaukee_Bucks_season" title="1989–90 Milwaukee Bucks season">Bucks</a> and <a href="/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_Philadelphia_76ers_season" title="1989–90 Philadelphia 76ers season">Philadelphia 76ers</a>. However, despite pushing the series to seven games, the Bulls lost to the <a href="/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_Detroit_Pistons_season" title="1989–90 Detroit Pistons season">Pistons</a> for the third consecutive season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nba.combio_42-6"><a href="#cite_note-nba.combio-42">[40]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="First_three-peat_.281991.E2.80.931993.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_three-peat_(1991–1993)">First three-peat (1991–1993)</span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_NBA_season" title="1990–91 NBA season">1990–91 season</a>, Jordan won his second MVP award after averaging 31.5 ppg on 53.9% shooting, 6.0 rpg, and 5.5 apg for the regular season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbb_29-6"><a href="#cite_note-dbb-29">[27]</a></sup> The Bulls finished in first place in their division for the first time in 16 years and set a franchise record with 61 wins in the regular season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbbulls_43-6"><a href="#cite_note-dbbulls-43">[41]</a></sup> With <a href="/wiki/Scottie_Pippen" title="Scottie Pippen">Scottie Pippen</a> developing into an All-Star, the Bulls had elevated their play. The Bulls defeated the <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_New_York_Knicks_season" title="1990–91 New York Knicks season">New York Knicks</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_Philadelphia_76ers_season" title="1990–91 Philadelphia 76ers season">Philadelphia 76ers</a> in the opening two rounds of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1991_NBA_Playoffs" title="1991 NBA Playoffs">the playoffs</a>. They advanced to the Eastern Conference Finals where their rival, the <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_Detroit_Pistons_season" title="1990–91 Detroit Pistons season">Detroit Pistons</a>, awaited them. However, this time the Bulls beat the Pistons in a four-game sweep.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1990–91_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-1990–91-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Bulls advanced to <a href="/wiki/1991_NBA_Finals" title="1991 NBA Finals">the NBA Finals</a> for the first time in franchise history to face the <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season" title="1990–91 Los Angeles Lakers season">Los Angeles Lakers</a>, who had <a href="/wiki/Magic_Johnson" title="Magic Johnson">Magic Johnson</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Worthy" title="James Worthy">James Worthy</a>, two formidable opponents. The Bulls won the series four games to one, and compiled a 15–2 playoff record along the way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1990–91_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-1990–91-56">[54]</a></sup> Perhaps the best known moment of the series came in Game 2 when, attempting a dunk, Jordan avoided a potential <a href="/wiki/Sam_Perkins" title="Sam Perkins">Sam Perkins</a> block by switching the ball from his right hand to his left in mid-air to lay the shot into the basket.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup> In his first Finals appearance, Jordan posted per game averages of 31.2 points on 56% shooting from the field, 11.4 assists, 6.6 rebounds, 2.8 steals, and 1.4 blocks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup> Jordan won his first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bill_Russell_NBA_Finals_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Bill Russell NBA Finals Most Valuable Player Award">NBA Finals MVP</a> award,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fnl_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-fnl-60">[58]</a></sup> and he cried while holding the NBA Finals trophy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-classicbio_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-classicbio-61">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jordan and the Bulls continued their dominance in the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_NBA_season" title="1991–92 NBA season">1991–92 season</a>, establishing a 67–15 record, topping their franchise record from 1990–91.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbbulls_43-7"><a href="#cite_note-dbbulls-43">[41]</a></sup> Jordan won his second consecutive MVP award with averages of 30.1 points, 6.4 rebounds and 6.1 assists per game on 52% shooting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MJ_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-MJ-50">[48]</a></sup> After winning a physical 7-game series over the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_New_York_Knicks_season" title="1991–92 New York Knicks season">New York Knicks</a> in the second round of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1992_NBA_Playoffs" title="1992 NBA Playoffs">the playoffs</a> and finishing off the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Cleveland_Cavaliers_season" title="1991–92 Cleveland Cavaliers season">Cleveland Cavaliers</a> in the Conference Finals in 6 games, the Bulls met <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Drexler" title="Clyde Drexler">Clyde Drexler</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Portland_Trail_Blazers_season" title="1991–92 Portland Trail Blazers season">Portland Trail Blazers</a> in <a href="/wiki/1992_NBA_Finals" title="1992 NBA Finals">the Finals</a>. The media, hoping to recreate a <a href="/wiki/Celtics%E2%80%93Lakers_rivalry" title="Celtics–Lakers rivalry">Magic–Bird rivalry</a>, highlighted the similarities between "Air" Jordan and Clyde "The Glide" during the pre-Finals hype.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sport-illustrated-cover_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-sport-illustrated-cover-62">[60]</a></sup> In the first game, Jordan scored a Finals-record 35 points in the first half, including a record-setting six <a href="/wiki/Three-point_field_goal" title="Three-point field goal">three-point field goals</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBA1991–92_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-NBA1991–92-63">[61]</a></sup> After the sixth three-pointer, he jogged down the court shrugging as he looked courtside. <a href="/wiki/Marv_Albert" title="Marv Albert">Marv Albert</a>, who broadcast the game, later stated that it was as if Jordan was saying, "I can't believe I'm doing this."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> The Bulls went on to win Game 1, and defeat the Blazers in six games. Jordan was named Finals MVP for the second year in a row<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fnl_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-fnl-60">[58]</a></sup> and finished the series averaging 35.8 ppg, 4.8 rpg, and 6.5 apg, while shooting 53% from the floor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fnl_60-2"><a href="#cite_note-fnl-60">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_NBA_season" title="1992–93 NBA season">1992–93 season</a>, despite a 32.6 ppg, 6.7 rpg, and 5.5 apg campaign and a second-place finish in Defensive Player of the Year voting,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MJ_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-MJ-50">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> Jordan's streak of consecutive MVP seasons ended as he lost the award to his friend <a href="/wiki/Charles_Barkley" title="Charles Barkley">Charles Barkley</a>. Coincidentally, Jordan and the Bulls met Barkley and his <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_Phoenix_Suns_season" title="1992–93 Phoenix Suns season">Phoenix Suns</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1993_NBA_Finals" title="1993 NBA Finals">1993 NBA Finals</a>. The Bulls won their third NBA championship on a game-winning shot by <a href="/wiki/John_Paxson" title="John Paxson">John Paxson</a> and a last-second block by <a href="/wiki/Horace_Grant" title="Horace Grant">Horace Grant</a>, but Jordan was once again Chicago's leader. He averaged a Finals-record 41.0 ppg during the six-game series,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> and became the first player in NBA history to win three straight Finals MVP awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fnl_60-3"><a href="#cite_note-fnl-60">[58]</a></sup> He scored more than 30 points in every game of the series, including 40 or more points in 4 consecutive games. With his third Finals triumph, Jordan capped off a seven-year run where he attained seven scoring titles and three championships, but there were signs that Jordan was tiring of his massive celebrity and all of the non-basketball hassles in his life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gambling">Gambling</span></h4>
<p>During the Bulls' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1993_NBA_Playoffs" title="1993 NBA Playoffs">playoff run in 1993</a>, Jordan was seen gambling in <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_City,_New_Jersey" title="Atlantic City, New Jersey">Atlantic City, New Jersey</a>, the night before a game against the <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_New_York_Knicks_season" title="1992–93 New York Knicks season">New York Knicks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> The previous year, he admitted that he had to cover $57,000 in gambling losses,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> and author Richard Esquinas wrote a book in 1993 claiming he had won $1.25 million from Jordan on the golf course.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA_Commissioner" title="NBA Commissioner">NBA Commissioner</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Stern" title="David Stern">David Stern</a> denied in 1995 and 2006 that Jordan's 1993 retirement was a secret suspension by the league for gambling,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vecsey19950319_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-vecsey19950319-71">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-simmons20060227_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-simmons20060227-72">[70]</a></sup> but the rumor spread widely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aroundtown20100823_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-aroundtown20100823-73">[71]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005, Jordan discussed his gambling with <a href="/wiki/Ed_Bradley" title="Ed Bradley">Ed Bradley</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/60_Minutes" title="60 Minutes">60 Minutes</a></i> and admitted that he made reckless decisions. Jordan stated, "Yeah, I've gotten myself into situations where I would not walk away and I've pushed the envelope. Is that compulsive? Yeah, it depends on how you look at it. If you're willing to jeopardize your livelihood and your family, then yeah". When Bradley asked him if his gambling ever got to the level where it jeopardized his livelihood or family, Jordan replied, "No".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-EB-74">[72]</a></sup> In 2010 <a href="/wiki/Ron_Shelton" title="Ron Shelton">Ron Shelton</a>, director of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jordan_Rides_the_Bus" title="Jordan Rides the Bus">Jordan Rides the Bus</a></i>, said that he began working on the documentary believing that the NBA had suspended him, but that research "convinced [him it] was nonsense".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aroundtown20100823_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-aroundtown20100823-73">[71]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="First_retirement_and_stint_in_Minor_League_Baseball_.281993.E2.80.931994.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_retirement_and_stint_in_Minor_League_Baseball_(1993–1994)">First retirement and stint in Minor League Baseball (1993–1994)</span></h3>
<table class="infobox bordered vcard" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th class="fn" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-size:larger; background-color:#DCDCDC;color:#000000;"><span class="note">Michael Jordan</span></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jordan_Scorpions.jpg"><img alt="Jordan Scorpions.jpg" data-file-height="529" data-file-width="536" decoding="async" height="276" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Jordan_Scorpions.jpg/280px-Jordan_Scorpions.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Jordan_Scorpions.jpg/420px-Jordan_Scorpions.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/25/Jordan_Scorpions.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a><div>Jordan in training with the <a href="/wiki/Scottsdale_Scorpions" title="Scottsdale Scorpions">Scottsdale Scorpions</a> in 1994</div></td></tr><tr style="background-color:#DCDCDC;color:#000000;"><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span class="note" style="font-weight:bold">Birmingham Barons – No. 45, 35</span></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/Outfielder" title="Outfielder">Outfielder</a></b></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><table style="width:100%; border:none;border-collapse:collapse;"><tbody><tr>
<td style="text-align:center;width:50%; border-width:0 1px 0 0;"><b>Batted:</b> Right</td>
<td style="text-align:center;width:50%; border-width:0 0 0 1px;"><b>Threw:</b> Right</td>
</tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="background-color:#DCDCDC;color:#000000;"><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Professional debut</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/Southern_League_(baseball)" title="Southern League (baseball)">Southern League</a>:</b> April 8, 1994, for the Birmingham Barons</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/Arizona_Fall_League" title="Arizona Fall League">Arizona Fall League</a>:</b> 1994, for the Scottsdale Scorpions</td></tr><tr style="background-color:#DCDCDC;color:#000000;"><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Last Southern League appearance</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">March 10, 1995, for the Birmingham Barons</td></tr><tr style="background-color:#DCDCDC;color:#000000;"><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Southern League statistics <br/>(through 1994)</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="text-align:right; width:50%; padding-right:0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Batting_average_(baseball)" title="Batting average (baseball)">Batting average</a></th><td style="width:50%; padding-left:0.5em;">.202</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="text-align:right; width:50%; padding-right:0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">Home runs</a></th><td style="width:50%; padding-left:0.5em;">3</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="text-align:right; width:50%; padding-right:0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Run_batted_in" title="Run batted in">Runs batted in</a></th><td style="width:50%; padding-left:0.5em;">51</td></tr><tr style="background-color:#DCDCDC;color:#000000;"><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Arizona Fall League statistics</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="text-align:right; width:50%; padding-right:0.5em;">Batting average</th><td style="width:50%; padding-left:0.5em;">.252</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="text-align:right; width:50%; padding-right:0.5em;">Runs batted in</th><td style="width:50%; padding-left:0.5em;">8</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><th colspan="2">
</th></tr><tr style="background-color:#DCDCDC;color:#000000;"><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Teams</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Barons" title="Birmingham Barons">Birmingham Barons</a> (1994–1995)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scottsdale_Scorpions" title="Scottsdale Scorpions">Scottsdale Scorpions</a> (1994)</li></ul>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>On October 6, 1993, Jordan announced his retirement, saying that he had lost his desire to play basketball. Jordan later said that the death of his father three months earlier had helped shape his decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> James Jordan was murdered on July 23, 1993, at a highway <a href="/wiki/Rest_area" title="Rest area">rest area</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lumberton,_North_Carolina" title="Lumberton, North Carolina">Lumberton, North Carolina</a>, by two teenagers, Daniel Green and Larry Martin Demery, who carjacked his <a href="/wiki/Lexus" title="Lexus">Lexus</a> bearing the license plate "UNC 0023".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-charged_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-charged-77">[75]</a></sup> His body, dumped in a South Carolina swamp, was not discovered until August 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-charged_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-charged-77">[75]</a></sup> Green and Demery were found after they made calls on James Jordan's cell phone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> convicted at trial, and sentenced to life in prison. Jordan was close to his father; as a child he had imitated the way his father stuck out his tongue while absorbed in work. He later adopted it as his own signature, often displaying it as he drove to the basket.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-9"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup> In 1996, he founded a Chicago-area <a href="/wiki/Boys_%26_Girls_Clubs_of_America" title="Boys &amp; Girls Clubs of America">Boys &amp; Girls Club</a> and dedicated it to his father.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-WP-79">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>In his 1998 autobiography <i>For the Love of the Game</i>, Jordan wrote that he had been preparing for retirement as early as the summer of 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> The added exhaustion due to the <a href="/wiki/1992_United_States_men%27s_Olympic_basketball_team" title="1992 United States men's Olympic basketball team">Dream Team</a> run in the <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">1992 Olympics</a> solidified Jordan's feelings about the game and his ever-growing celebrity status. Jordan's announcement sent shock waves throughout the NBA and appeared on the front pages of newspapers around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jordan further surprised the sports world by signing a <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">Minor League Baseball</a> contract with the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> on February 7, 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup> He reported to <a href="/wiki/Spring_training" title="Spring training">spring training</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sarasota,_Florida" title="Sarasota, Florida">Sarasota, Florida</a>, and was assigned to the team's minor league system on March 31, 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronology_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-chronology-84">[82]</a></sup> Jordan has said this decision was made to pursue the dream of his late father, who had always envisioned his son as a <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> player.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> The White Sox were owned by Bulls owner <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Reinsdorf" title="Jerry Reinsdorf">Jerry Reinsdorf</a>, who continued to honor Jordan's basketball contract during the years he played baseball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1994, Jordan played for the <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Barons" title="Birmingham Barons">Birmingham Barons</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Double-A_(baseball)" title="Double-A (baseball)">Double-A</a> minor league affiliate of the Chicago White Sox, <a href="/wiki/Batting_average_(baseball)" title="Batting average (baseball)">batting</a> .202 with three <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home runs</a>, 51 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Runs_batted_in" title="Runs batted in">runs batted in</a>, 30 <a href="/wiki/Stolen_base" title="Stolen base">stolen bases</a>, 114 <a href="/wiki/Strikeout" title="Strikeout">strikeouts</a>, 51 <a href="/wiki/Base_on_balls" title="Base on balls">bases on balls</a>, and 11 <a href="/wiki/Error_(baseball)" title="Error (baseball)">errors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> He also appeared for the <a href="/wiki/Scottsdale_Scorpions" title="Scottsdale Scorpions">Scottsdale Scorpions</a> in the 1994 <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Fall_League" title="Arizona Fall League">Arizona Fall League</a>, batting .252 against the top prospects in baseball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronology_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-chronology-84">[82]</a></sup> On November 1, 1994, his number 23 was retired by the Bulls in a ceremony that included the erection of a permanent sculpture known as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_Jordan_statue" title="Michael Jordan statue">The Spirit</a></i> outside the new <a href="/wiki/United_Center" title="United Center">United Center</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MJS_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-MJS-89">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTLTL_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-JTLTL-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id=".22I.27m_back.22:_Return_to_the_NBA_.281995.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;I'm_back&quot;:_Return_to_the_NBA_(1995)">"I'm back": Return to the NBA (1995)</span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_NBA_season" title="1993–94 NBA season">1993–94 season</a>, the Bulls achieved a 55–27 record without Jordan in the lineup,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbbulls_43-8"><a href="#cite_note-dbbulls-43">[41]</a></sup> and lost to the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_New_York_Knicks_season" title="1993–94 New York Knicks season">New York Knicks</a> in the second round of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1994_NBA_Playoffs" title="1994 NBA Playoffs">the playoffs</a>. The <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Chicago_Bulls_season" title="1994–95 Chicago Bulls season">1994–95 Bulls</a> were a shell of the championship team of just two years earlier. Struggling at mid-season to ensure a spot in the playoffs, Chicago was 31–31 at one point in mid-March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> The team received help, however, when Jordan decided to return to the Bulls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 1995, Jordan decided to quit baseball because he feared he might become a <a href="/wiki/Replacement_player" title="Replacement player">replacement player</a> during the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1994–95 Major League Baseball strike">Major League Baseball strike</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> On March 18, 1995, Jordan announced his return to the NBA through a two-word press release: "I'm back."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-10"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup> The next day, Jordan took to the court with the Bulls to face the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Indiana_Pacers_season" title="1994–95 Indiana Pacers season">Indiana Pacers</a> in <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>, scoring 19 points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-returns_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-returns-95">[93]</a></sup> The game had the highest <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_ratings" title="Nielsen ratings">Nielsen rating</a> of any regular season NBA game since 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup> Although he could have worn his normal number even though the Bulls retired it, Jordan wore number 45, his baseball number.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-returns_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-returns-95">[93]</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite his 18-month hiatus from the NBA, Jordan played well, making a game-winning jump shot against <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Atlanta_Hawks_season" title="1994–95 Atlanta Hawks season">Atlanta</a> in his fourth game back. He scored 55 points in his next game, against the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_New_York_Knicks_season" title="1994–95 New York Knicks season">Knicks</a> at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> on March 28, 1995.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nba.combio_42-7"><a href="#cite_note-nba.combio-42">[40]</a></sup> Boosted by Jordan's comeback, the Bulls went 13–4 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1995_NBA_Playoffs" title="1995 NBA Playoffs">to make the playoffs</a> and advanced to the Eastern Conference Semifinals against the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Orlando_Magic_season" title="1994–95 Orlando Magic season">Orlando Magic</a>. At the end of Game 1, Orlando's <a href="/wiki/Nick_Anderson" title="Nick Anderson">Nick Anderson</a> stripped Jordan from behind, leading to the game-winning basket for the Magic; he would later comment that Jordan "didn't look like the old Michael Jordan"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup> and that "No. 45 doesn't explode like No. 23 used to."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-No23_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-No23-98">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jordan responded by scoring 38 points in the next game, which Chicago won. Before the game, Jordan decided that he would immediately resume wearing his former number, 23. The Bulls were fined $25,000 for failing to report the impromptu number change to the NBA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-No23_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-No23-98">[96]</a></sup> Jordan was fined an additional $5,000 for opting to wear white sneakers when the rest of the Bulls wore black.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> He averaged 31 points per game in the series, but Orlando won the series in six games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-br_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-br-31">[29]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Second_three-peat_.281995.E2.80.931998.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_three-peat_(1995–1998)">Second three-peat (1995–1998)</span></h3>
<p>Jordan was freshly motivated by the playoff defeat, and he trained aggressively for the <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_NBA_season" title="1995–96 NBA season">1995–96 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup> The Bulls were strengthened by the addition of rebound specialist <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Rodman" title="Dennis Rodman">Dennis Rodman</a>, and the team dominated the league, starting the season at 41–3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1995–96_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-1995–96-101">[99]</a></sup> The Bulls eventually finished with the <a href="/wiki/List_of_NBA_teams_by_single_season_win_percentage" title="List of NBA teams by single season win percentage">best regular season record</a> in NBA history, 72–10, a mark broken two decades later by the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Golden_State_Warriors_season" title="2015–16 Golden State Warriors season">2015–16 Golden State Warriors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> Jordan led the league in scoring with 30.4 ppg<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup> and won the league's regular-season and All-Star Game MVP awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-11"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1996_NBA_Playoffs" title="1996 NBA Playoffs">the playoffs</a>, the Bulls lost only three games in four series (<a href="/wiki/Miami_Heat" title="Miami Heat">Miami Heat</a> 3–0, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">New York Knicks</a> 4–1, <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Magic" title="Orlando Magic">Orlando Magic</a> 4–0). They defeated the <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_Seattle_SuperSonics_season" title="1995–96 Seattle SuperSonics season">Seattle SuperSonics</a> 4–2 in the <a href="/wiki/1996_NBA_Finals" title="1996 NBA Finals">NBA Finals</a> to win their fourth championship. Jordan was named Finals MVP for a record fourth time,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fnl_60-4"><a href="#cite_note-fnl-60">[58]</a></sup> surpassing <a href="/wiki/Magic_Johnson" title="Magic Johnson">Magic Johnson</a>'s three Finals MVP awards. He also achieved only the second sweep of the MVP Awards in the All-Star Game, regular season, and NBA Finals, after <a href="/wiki/Willis_Reed" title="Willis Reed">Willis Reed</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1969%E2%80%9370_NBA_season" title="1969–70 NBA season">1969–70 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nba.combio_42-8"><a href="#cite_note-nba.combio-42">[40]</a></sup> Upon winning the championship, his first since his father's murder, Jordan reacted emotionally, clutching the game ball and crying on the locker room floor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-12"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-classicbio_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-classicbio-61">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_NBA_season" title="1996–97 NBA season">1996–97 season</a>, the Bulls started out 69–11, but missed out on a second consecutive 70-win season by losing their final two games to finish 69–13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1996–97_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-1996–97-104">[102]</a></sup> However, Jordan was beaten for the NBA MVP Award by <a href="/wiki/Karl_Malone" title="Karl Malone">Karl Malone</a>. The Bulls again advanced to <a href="/wiki/1997_NBA_Finals" title="1997 NBA Finals">the Finals</a>, where they faced Malone's <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_Utah_Jazz_season" title="1996–97 Utah Jazz season">Utah Jazz</a>. The series against the Jazz featured two of the more memorable clutch moments of Jordan's career. He won Game 1 for the Bulls with a <a href="/wiki/Buzzer_beater" title="Buzzer beater">buzzer-beating</a> jump shot. In Game 5, with the series tied at 2, Jordan played despite being feverish and dehydrated from a stomach virus. In what is known as the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flu_game" title="Flu game">Flu Game</a>", Jordan scored 38 points, including the game-deciding 3-pointer with 25 seconds remaining.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup> The Bulls won 90–88 and went on to win the series in six games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1996–97_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-1996–97-104">[102]</a></sup> For the fifth time in as many Finals appearances, Jordan received the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bill_Russell_NBA_Finals_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Bill Russell NBA Finals Most Valuable Player Award">Finals MVP award</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fnl_60-5"><a href="#cite_note-fnl-60">[58]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/1997_NBA_All-Star_Game" title="1997 NBA All-Star Game">1997 NBA All-Star Game</a>, Jordan posted the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Triple_double" title="Triple double">triple double</a> in All-Star Game history in a victorious effort; however, he did not receive the MVP award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phil_Jackson_Lipofsky.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="282" decoding="async" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Phil_Jackson_Lipofsky.JPG/170px-Phil_Jackson_Lipofsky.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Phil_Jackson_Lipofsky.JPG/255px-Phil_Jackson_Lipofsky.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9e/Phil_Jackson_Lipofsky.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phil_Jackson_Lipofsky.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jordan with coach <a href="/wiki/Phil_Jackson" title="Phil Jackson">Phil Jackson</a>, 1997</div></div></div>
<p>Jordan and the Bulls compiled a 62–20 record in the <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_NBA_season" title="1997–98 NBA season">1997–98 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbbulls_43-9"><a href="#cite_note-dbbulls-43">[41]</a></sup> Jordan led the league with 28.7 points per game,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MJ_50-3"><a href="#cite_note-MJ-50">[48]</a></sup> securing his fifth regular-season MVP award, plus honors for All-NBA First Team, First Defensive Team and the All-Star Game MVP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-13"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup> The Bulls won the Eastern Conference Championship for a third straight season, including surviving a seven-game series with the <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_Indiana_Pacers_season" title="1997–98 Indiana Pacers season">Indiana Pacers</a> in the Eastern Conference Finals; it was the first time Jordan had played in a Game 7 since the 1992 Eastern Conference Semifinals with the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_New_York_Knicks_season" title="1991–92 New York Knicks season">Knicks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> After winning, they moved on for a rematch with the <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_Utah_Jazz_season" title="1997–98 Utah Jazz season">Jazz</a> in <a href="/wiki/1998_NBA_Finals" title="1998 NBA Finals">the Finals</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Bulls returned to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delta_Center" title="Delta Center">Delta Center</a> for <a href="/wiki/Game_6_of_the_1998_NBA_Finals" title="Game 6 of the 1998 NBA Finals">Game 6</a> on June 14, 1998, leading the series 3–2. Jordan executed a series of plays, considered to be one of the greatest clutch performances in NBA Finals history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clutch1998_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-clutch1998-110">[108]</a></sup> With 41.9 seconds remaining and the Bulls trailing 86–83, Phil Jackson called a timeout. When play resumed, Jordan received the inbound pass, drove to the basket, and sank a shot over several Jazz defenders, cutting Utah's lead to 86–85.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clutch1998_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-clutch1998-110">[108]</a></sup> The Jazz brought the ball upcourt and passed the ball to Malone, who was set up in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_post" title="Low post">low post</a> and was being guarded by Rodman. Malone jostled with Rodman and caught the pass, but Jordan cut behind him and stole the ball out of his hands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clutch1998_110-2"><a href="#cite_note-clutch1998-110">[108]</a></sup> Jordan then dribbled down the court and paused, eyeing his defender, Jazz guard <a href="/wiki/Bryon_Russell" title="Bryon Russell">Bryon Russell</a>. With 10 seconds remaining, Jordan started to dribble right, then crossed over to his left, possibly pushing off Russell,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> although the officials did not call a <a href="/wiki/Personal_foul_(basketball)" title="Personal foul (basketball)">foul</a>. With 5.2 seconds left, Jordan made the climactic shot of his Bulls career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> He gave Chicago an 87–86 lead with a jumper over Russell. Afterwards, the Jazz' John Stockton narrowly missed a game-winning three-pointer. The buzzer sounded, and Jordan and the Bulls won their sixth NBA championship,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> achieving a second three-peat in the decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> Once again, Jordan was voted Finals MVP,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fnl_60-6"><a href="#cite_note-fnl-60">[58]</a></sup> having led all scorers by averaging 33.5 points per game, including 45 in the deciding Game 6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> Jordan's six Finals MVPs is a record; <a href="/wiki/LeBron_James" title="LeBron James">LeBron James</a> is in second place with four.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> The 1998 Finals holds the highest television rating of any Finals series in history. Game 6 also holds the highest television rating of any game in NBA history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Second_retirement_.281999.E2.80.932001.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_retirement_(1999–2001)">Second retirement (1999–2001)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michael_Jordan_Achievements.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Michael_Jordan_Achievements.jpg/220px-Michael_Jordan_Achievements.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Michael_Jordan_Achievements.jpg/330px-Michael_Jordan_Achievements.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Michael_Jordan_Achievements.jpg/440px-Michael_Jordan_Achievements.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michael_Jordan_Achievements.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Plaque at the United Center that chronicles Jordan's career achievements</div></div></div>
<p>With <a href="/wiki/Phil_Jackson" title="Phil Jackson">Phil Jackson</a>'s contract expiring, the pending departures of <a href="/wiki/Scottie_Pippen" title="Scottie Pippen">Scottie Pippen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Rodman" title="Dennis Rodman">Dennis Rodman</a> looming, and being in the latter stages of an owner-induced <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_NBA_lockout" title="1998–99 NBA lockout">lockout</a> of NBA players, Jordan retired for the second time on January 13, 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup> On January 19, 2000, Jordan returned to the NBA not as a player, but as part owner and president of basketball operations for the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Wizards" title="Washington Wizards">Washington Wizards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> Jordan's responsibilities with the Wizards were comprehensive. He controlled all aspects of the Wizards' basketball operations, and had the final say in all personnel matters. Opinions of Jordan as a basketball executive were mixed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pollin_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pollin-125">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brady_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brady-126">[124]</a></sup> He managed to purge the team of several highly paid, unpopular players (such as forward <a href="/wiki/Juwan_Howard" title="Juwan Howard">Juwan Howard</a> and point guard <a href="/wiki/Rod_Strickland" title="Rod Strickland">Rod Strickland</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> but used the first pick in the <a href="/wiki/2001_NBA_draft" title="2001 NBA draft">2001 NBA draft</a> to select high schooler <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Brown" title="Kwame Brown">Kwame Brown</a>, who did not live up to expectations and was traded away after four seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pollin_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pollin-125">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilbon_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wilbon-129">[127]</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite his January 1999 claim that he was "99.9% certain" that he would never play another NBA game,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-classicbio_61-2"><a href="#cite_note-classicbio-61">[59]</a></sup> in the summer of 2001 Jordan expressed interest in making another comeback,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ha-nytimes_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-ha-nytimes-130">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jwhite-cbc_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-jwhite-cbc-131">[129]</a></sup> this time with his new team. Inspired by the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">NHL</a> comeback of his friend <a href="/wiki/Mario_Lemieux" title="Mario Lemieux">Mario Lemieux</a> the previous winter,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup> Jordan spent much of the spring and summer of 2001 in training, holding several invitation-only camps for NBA players in Chicago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-comebackcamp_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-comebackcamp-133">[131]</a></sup> In addition, Jordan hired his old Chicago Bulls head coach, <a href="/wiki/Doug_Collins_(basketball)" title="Doug Collins (basketball)">Doug Collins</a>, as Washington's coach for the upcoming season, a decision that many saw as foreshadowing another Jordan return.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ha-nytimes_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-ha-nytimes-130">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jwhite-cbc_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-jwhite-cbc-131">[129]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Washington_Wizards_comeback_.282001.E2.80.932003.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Washington_Wizards_comeback_(2001–2003)">Washington Wizards comeback (2001–2003)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MichaelJordanDepOfDefense.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="531" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/MichaelJordanDepOfDefense.jpg/220px-MichaelJordanDepOfDefense.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/MichaelJordanDepOfDefense.jpg/330px-MichaelJordanDepOfDefense.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/MichaelJordanDepOfDefense.jpg/440px-MichaelJordanDepOfDefense.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MichaelJordanDepOfDefense.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jordan as a member of the Washington Wizards, April 14, 2003</div></div></div>
<p>On September 25, 2001, Jordan announced his return to the NBA to play for the Washington Wizards, indicating his intention to donate his salary as a player to a relief effort for the victims of the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> In an injury-plagued <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_NBA_season" title="2001–02 NBA season">2001–02 season</a>, he led the team in scoring (22.9 ppg), assists (5.2 apg), and steals (1.42 spg).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-14"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup> However, torn <a href="/wiki/Cartilage" title="Cartilage">cartilage</a> in his right knee ended Jordan's season after only 60 games, the fewest he had played in a regular season since playing 17 games after returning from his first retirement during the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_NBA_season" title="1994–95 NBA season">1994–95 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbb_29-7"><a href="#cite_note-dbb-29">[27]</a></sup> Jordan started 53 of his 60 games for the season, averaging 24.3 points, 5.4 assists, and 6.0 rebounds, and shooting 41.9% from the field in his 53 starts. His last seven appearances were in a reserve role, in which he averaged just over 20 minutes per game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup>
</p><p>Playing in his 14th and final NBA All-Star Game in <a href="/wiki/2003_NBA_All-Star_Game" title="2003 NBA All-Star Game">2003</a>, Jordan passed <a href="/wiki/Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar" title="Kareem Abdul-Jabbar">Kareem Abdul-Jabbar</a> as the all-time leading scorer in All-Star Game history (a record since broken by <a href="/wiki/LeBron_James" title="LeBron James">LeBron James</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kobe_Bryant" title="Kobe Bryant">Kobe Bryant</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup> That year, Jordan was the only Washington player to play in all 82 games, starting in 67 of them. He averaged 20.0 points, 6.1 rebounds, 3.8 assists, and 1.5 steals per game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-15"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup> He also shot 45% from the field, and 82% from the free throw line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbah_5-16"><a href="#cite_note-nbah-5">[5]</a></sup> Even though he turned 40 during the season, he scored 20 or more points 42 times, 30 or more points nine times, and 40 or more points three times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nba.combio_42-9"><a href="#cite_note-nba.combio-42">[40]</a></sup> On February 21, 2003, Jordan became the first 40-year-old to tally 43 points in an NBA game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> During his stint with the Wizards, all of Jordan's home games at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MCI_Center" title="MCI Center">MCI Center</a> were sold out, and the Wizards were the second most-watched team in the NBA, averaging 20,172 fans a game at home and 19,311 on the road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup> However, neither of Jordan's final two seasons resulted in a playoff appearance for the Wizards, and Jordan was often unsatisfied with the play of those around him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rob_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rob-141">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chemistry_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chemistry-142">[140]</a></sup> At several points he openly criticized his teammates to the media, citing their lack of focus and
